	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Britney Spears</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>Britney Jean Spears</b> (born December 2, 1981) is an American singer, songwriter, dancer, and actress. Born in <a href="/wiki/McComb,_Mississippi" title="McComb, Mississippi">McComb, Mississippi</a> and raised in <a href="/wiki/Kentwood,_Louisiana" title="Kentwood, Louisiana">Kentwood, Louisiana</a>, she appeared in stage productions and television series, before signing with <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> in 1997. Spears's first two studio albums, <i><a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)" title="...Baby One More Time (album)">...Baby One More Time</a></i> (1999) and <i><a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_(album)" title="Oops!... I Did It Again (album)">Oops!... I Did It Again</a></i> (2000), were global successes and made her the best-selling teenage artist of all-time. Referred to as the "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Princess of Pop</a>", Spears is regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Pop_icon" title="Pop icon">pop icon</a> and is credited with influencing the revival of <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> during the late 1990s and early 2000s.
</p><p>Spears adopted more mature and provocative themes for her next two studio albums, <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_(album)" title="Britney (album)">Britney</a></i> (2001) and <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Zone" title="In the Zone">In the Zone</a></i> (2003), and made her feature film debut in a starring role in <i><a href="/wiki/Crossroads_(2002_film)" title="Crossroads (2002 film)">Crossroads</a></i> (2002). Following a series of heavily publicized personal struggles and erratic public behavior, Spears's career was interrupted, before the release of her fifth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Blackout_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Blackout (Britney Spears album)">Blackout</a></i> (2007), which is often critically referred to as her best work.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Her erratic behavior and hospitalizations led Spears to be placed on a still ongoing <a href="/wiki/Conservatorship" title="Conservatorship">conservatorship</a>. She returned to the top of record charts with her sixth and seventh studio albums, <i><a href="/wiki/Circus_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Circus (Britney Spears album)">Circus</a></i> (2008) and <i><a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Femme Fatale (Britney Spears album)">Femme Fatale</a></i> (2011), respectively. In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> reported that Spears was the highest paid female musician of the year, with earnings of $58&#160;million, having last topped the list in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> During the promotion of her eighth and ninth studio albums, <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_Jean" title="Britney Jean">Britney Jean</a></i> (2013) and <i><a href="/wiki/Glory_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Glory (Britney Spears album)">Glory</a></i> (2016), Spears embarked on a four-year <a href="/wiki/Concert_residency" title="Concert residency">concert residency</a>, <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Planet_Hollywood_Resort_%26_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Planet Hollywood Resort &amp; Casino">Planet Hollywood Resort &amp; Casino</a> in Las Vegas, which became one of the highest-grossing residencies of all-time. In 2019, Spears announced an indefinite career hiatus and was later admitted involuntarily into a mental health facility by her <a href="/wiki/Conservatorship" title="Conservatorship">conservator</a>, leading to a court-led investigation into malpractice conducted by Spears's team.
</p><p>Spears has scored six number one albums on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, making her the third best performing female artist on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_472190_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_472190-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Five of Spears's singles have reached number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>: "<a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">...Baby One More Time</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Womanizer_(song)" title="Womanizer (song)">Womanizer</a>", "<a href="/wiki/3_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="3 (Britney Spears song)">3</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Hold_It_Against_Me" title="Hold It Against Me">Hold It Against Me</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/S%26M_(song)" title="S&amp;M (song)">S&amp;M</a>". Other singles, "<a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_(song)" title="Oops!... I Did It Again (song)">Oops!... I Did It Again</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>", topped the charts in most countries. With "3" in 2009 and "Hold It Against Me" in 2011, she became the second artist after <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> in the Hot 100's history to debut at number one with two or more songs. Spears has earned <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Britney_Spears" title="List of awards and nominations received by Britney Spears">numerous awards</a> and accolades, including a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>; seven <a href="/wiki/Guinness_Book_of_World_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Guinness Book of World Records">Guinness World Records</a>; six <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson_Video_Vanguard_Award" title="Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award">Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award</a>; seven <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Award" title="Billboard Music Award"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a>, including the Millennium Award;<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> the inaugural Radio Disney Icon Award; and a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><i>Billboard</i> ranked her as the eighth-biggest artist of the 2000s decade.<sup id="cite_ref-bbad_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbad-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> One of the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists</a>, Spears has sold 150 million records worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-billboard150_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard150-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> including over 70 million records in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-usrecordsales_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usrecordsales-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-records_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, Spears is the fourth best-selling female album artist of the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> era<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> as well as the best-selling female album artist of the 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-21sells_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21sells-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Spears launched a <a href="/wiki/List_of_celebrity-branded_perfumes" title="List of celebrity-branded perfumes">perfume brand</a> with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Arden,_Inc." title="Elizabeth Arden, Inc.">Elizabeth Arden, Inc.</a>; sales exceeded US$1.5&#160;billion as of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Britney_Spears&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Spears has topped the list of most searched celebrities seven times in 12 years, a record since the inception of the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<h3><span id="1981.E2.80.931997:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1981‚Äì1997:_Early_life_and_career_beginnings">1981‚Äì1997: Early life and career beginnings</span></h3>
<p>Britney Jean Spears was born on December 2, 1981 in <a href="/wiki/McComb,_Mississippi" title="McComb, Mississippi">McComb, Mississippi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bsbiography_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bsbiography-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> the second child of <a href="/wiki/Lynne_Spears" title="Lynne Spears">Lynne Irene Bridges</a> and James Parnell Spears. Her maternal grandmother, Lillian Portell, was English (born in London), and one of Spears's maternal great-great-grandfathers was Maltese.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Her siblings are <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Spears" title="Bryan Spears">Bryan James</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Lynn_Spears" title="Jamie Lynn Spears">Jamie Lynn Spears</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> She was born in the <a href="/wiki/Bible_Belt" title="Bible Belt">Bible Belt</a>, where socially conservative <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Protestantism" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelical Protestantism">evangelical Protestantism</a> is a particularly strong religious influence.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Spears was baptized as a <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Baptist">Southern Baptist</a>. As an adult, she has studied  <a href="/wiki/Kabbalist" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabbalist">Kabbalist</a> teachings.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> She sang in a <a href="/wiki/Baptist" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> church choir as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At age three, she started attending dance lessons in her hometown of <a href="/wiki/Kentwood,_Louisiana" title="Kentwood, Louisiana">Kentwood, Louisiana</a>, and was selected to perform as a solo artist at the annual recital. Spears made her local stage debut at age five, singing "<a href="/wiki/What_Child_Is_This%3F" title="What Child Is This?">What Child Is This?</a>" at her <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> graduation. During her childhood, she also had gymnastics and voice lessons, and won many state-level competitions and children's talent shows.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rs1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She said about her ambition as a child, "I was in my own world, [...] I found out what I'm supposed to do at an early age".<sup id="cite_ref-rs1_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At age eight, Spears and her mother Lynne traveled to <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, Georgia to audition for the 1990s revival of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mickey_Mouse_Club" title="The Mickey Mouse Club">The Mickey Mouse Club</a></i>. Casting director Matt Casella rejected her as too young, but introduced her to Nancy Carson, a New York City talent agent. Carson was impressed with Spears's singing and suggested enrolling her at the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Performing_Arts_School" title="Professional Performing Arts School">Professional Performing Arts School</a>; shortly after, Lynne and her daughters moved to a sublet apartment in New York.
</p><p>Spears was hired for her first professional role as the understudy for the lead role of Tina Denmark in the Off-Broadway musical <i><a href="/wiki/Ruthless!" title="Ruthless!">Ruthless!</a></i>. She also appeared as a contestant on the popular television show <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Search" title="Star Search">Star Search</a></i> and was cast in a number of commercials.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In December 1992, she was cast in <i>The Mickey Mouse Club</i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Gosling" title="Ryan Gosling">Ryan Gosling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Keri_Russell" title="Keri Russell">Keri Russell</a>. After the show was canceled in 1996, she returned to Mississippi and enrolled at McComb's <a href="/wiki/Parklane_Academy" title="Parklane Academy">Parklane Academy</a>. Although she made friends with most of her classmates, she compared the school to "the opening scene in <i><a href="/wiki/Clueless_(film)" title="Clueless (film)">Clueless</a></i> with all the <a href="/wiki/Cliques" class="mw-redirect" title="Cliques">cliques</a>. [...] I was so bored. I was the point guard on the basketball team. I had my boyfriend, and I went to homecoming and Christmas formal. But I wanted more."<sup id="cite_ref-rs1_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rs2_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 1997, Spears was in talks with manager <a href="/wiki/Lou_Pearlman" title="Lou Pearlman">Lou Pearlman</a> to join the female pop group <a href="/wiki/Innosense" title="Innosense">Innosense</a>. Lynne asked family friend and entertainment lawyer <a href="/wiki/Larry_Rudolph" title="Larry Rudolph">Larry Rudolph</a> for his opinion and submitted a tape of Spears singing over a <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a> karaoke song along with some pictures. Rudolph decided that he wanted to pitch her to record labels, for which she needed a professional demo made. He sent Spears an unused song of <a href="/wiki/Toni_Braxton" title="Toni Braxton">Toni Braxton</a>; she rehearsed for a week and recorded her vocals in a studio with a <a href="/wiki/Audio_engineer" title="Audio engineer">sound engineer</a>. Spears traveled to New York with the demo and met with executives from four labels, returning to Kentwood the same day. Three of the labels rejected her, saying that audiences wanted pop bands such as the <a href="/wiki/Backstreet_Boys" title="Backstreet Boys">Backstreet Boys</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spice_Girls" title="Spice Girls">Spice Girls</a>, and "there wasn't going to be another <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, another <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Gibson" title="Debbie Gibson">Debbie Gibson</a>, or another <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_(American_singer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiffany (American singer)">Tiffany</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-hughes145_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two weeks later, executives from <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> returned calls to Rudolph.<sup id="cite_ref-hughes145_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Senior vice president of <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> Jeff Fenster said about Spears's audition that "it's very rare to hear someone that age who can deliver emotional content and commercial appeal...For any artist, the motivation‚Äîthe 'eye of the tiger'‚Äîis extremely important. And Britney had that."<sup id="cite_ref-rs1_24-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Spears sang Houston's "<a href="/wiki/I_Have_Nothing" title="I Have Nothing">I Have Nothing</a>" (1992) for the executives, and was subsequently signed to the label.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> They appointed her to work with producer Eric Foster White for a month, who reportedly shaped her voice from "lower and less poppy" delivery to "distinctively, unmistakably Britney."<sup id="cite_ref-Hughes_2005_147_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes_2005_147-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> After hearing the recorded material, president <a href="/wiki/Clive_Calder" title="Clive Calder">Clive Calder</a> ordered a full album. Spears had originally envisioned "<a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a> music, but younger; more adult contemporary." She felt secure with her label's appointment of producers, since "It made more sense to go pop, because I can dance to it‚Äîit's more me."<sup id="cite_ref-rs1_24-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> She flew to <a href="/wiki/Cheiron_Studios" title="Cheiron Studios">Cheiron Studios</a> in Stockholm, Sweden, where half of the album was recorded from March to April 1998, with producers <a href="/wiki/Max_Martin" title="Max Martin">Max Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denniz_Pop" title="Denniz Pop">Denniz Pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rami_Yacoub" title="Rami Yacoub">Rami Yacoub</a>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-rs1_24-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs1-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.932000:_...Baby_One_More_Time_and_Oops.21..._I_Did_It_Again"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998‚Äì2000:_...Baby_One_More_Time_and_Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again">1998‚Äì2000: <i>...Baby One More Time</i> and <i>Oops!... I Did It Again</i></span></h3>
<p>After Spears returned to the United States, she embarked on a shopping mall promotional tour to promote her upcoming debut album. Her show was a four-song set and she was accompanied by two back-up dancers. Her first concert tour followed, as an opening act for <a href="/wiki/NSYNC" title="NSYNC">NSYNC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Her debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)" title="...Baby One More Time (album)">...Baby One More Time</a></i>, was released on January 12, 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> It debuted at number one on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was certified two-times <a href="/wiki/Music_recording_sales_certification" class="mw-redirect" title="Music recording sales certification">platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> after a month. Worldwide, the album topped the charts in fifteen countries and sold over 10 million copies in a year.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> It became the biggest-selling album ever by a teenage artist.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(song)" title="...Baby One More Time (song)">title track</a> was released as the <a href="/wiki/Lead_single" title="Lead single">lead single</a> from the album. Originally, Jive Records wanted its music video to be animated; however, Spears rejected it, and suggested the final concept of a Catholic schoolgirl.<sup id="cite_ref-Hughes_2005_147_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hughes_2005_147-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The single sold 500,000 copies on its first day, and peaked at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, topping the chart for two consecutive weeks. It has sold more than 10 million copies, making it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_singles" title="List of best-selling singles">best-selling singles</a> of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> "...Baby One More Time" later received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> nomination for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The title track also topped the singles chart for two weeks in the United Kingdom, and became the fastest-selling single ever by a female artist, shipping over 460,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> It would later become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_million-selling_singles_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of million-selling singles in the United Kingdom">25th-most successful song of all time in British chart history</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Spears is the youngest female artist to have a million seller in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-ukchart_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukchart-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/(You_Drive_Me)_Crazy" title="(You Drive Me) Crazy">(You Drive Me) Crazy</a>" was released as the third single from the album. It became a top-ten hit worldwide and further propelled the success of the <i><a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)" title="...Baby One More Time (album)">...Baby One More Time</a></i> album. The album has sold 25 million copies worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> making it one of the best-selling albums of all time. It is the best-selling debut album by any artist.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 28, 1999, Spears began her first headlining <a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_Tour" title="...Baby One More Time Tour">...Baby One More Time Tour</a> in North America, which was positively received by critics.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> It also generated some controversy due to her racy outfits.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> An extension of the tour, titled Crazy 2k, followed in March 2000. Spears premiered songs from her upcoming second album during the show.<sup id="cite_ref-rs2_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rs2-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_(album)" title="Oops!... I Did It Again (album)">Oops!... I Did It Again</a></i>, her second studio album, was released in May 2000. It debuted at number one in the US, selling 1.3 million copies, breaking the <a href="/wiki/SoundScan" class="mw-redirect" title="SoundScan">SoundScan</a> record for the highest debut sales by any solo artist.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> The album has sold over 20 million copies worldwide to date,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> making it one of the best-selling albums of all time. <a href="/wiki/Rob_Sheffield" title="Rob Sheffield">Rob Sheffield</a> of <i>Rolling Stone</i> said that "the great thing about <i>Oops!</i>&#160;‚Äì under the cheese surface, Britney's demand for satisfaction is complex, fierce and downright scary, making her a true child of <a href="/wiki/Rock_%26_roll" class="mw-redirect" title="Rock &amp; roll">rock &amp; roll</a> tradition."<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The album's lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_(song)" title="Oops!... I Did It Again (song)">Oops!... I Did It Again</a>", peaked at the top of the charts in Australia, New Zealand, the United Kingdom and many other European nations.<sup id="cite_ref-ukchart_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukchart-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The album as well as the title track received Grammy nominations for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Best Pop Vocal Album</a> and Best Female Pop Vocal Performance, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The same year, Spears embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_Tour" title="Oops!... I Did It Again Tour">Oops!... I Did It Again Tour</a>, which grossed $40.5 million; she also released her first book, <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears_products" title="Britney Spears products">Britney Spears' Heart to Heart</a></i>, co-written with her mother.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On September 7, 2000, Spears performed at the <a href="/wiki/2000_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2000 MTV Video Music Awards">2000 MTV Video Music Awards</a>. Halfway through the performance, she ripped off her black suit to reveal a sequined flesh-colored bodysuit, followed by heavy dance routine. It is noted by critics as the moment that Spears showed signs of becoming a more provocative performer.<sup id="cite_ref-vma_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vma-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Amidst media speculation, Spears confirmed she was dating NSYNC member <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Spears and Timberlake would both graduate high school via <a href="/wiki/Distance_learning" class="mw-redirect" title="Distance learning">distance learning</a> from the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska_High_School" title="University of Nebraska High School">University of Nebraska High School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DN_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DN-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ehigh_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ehigh-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> She also bought a home in <a href="/wiki/Destin,_Florida" title="Destin, Florida">Destin, Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2001.E2.80.932002:_Britney_and_Crossroads"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001‚Äì2002:_Britney_and_Crossroads">2001‚Äì2002: <i>Britney</i> and <i>Crossroads</i></span></h3>
<p>In February 2001, Spears signed a $7‚Äì8&#160;million promotional deal with <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>, and released another book co-written with her mother, titled <i>A Mother's Gift</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Her self-titled third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_(album)" title="Britney (album)">Britney</a></i>, was released in November 2001. While on tour, she felt inspired by hip hop artists such as <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a> and wanted to create a record with a funkier sound.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The album debuted at number one in the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and reached top five positions in Australia, the United Kingdom and mainland Europe and sold over 15 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-ukchart_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ukchart-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wwsales2013_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wwsales2013-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> called <i>Britney</i> "the record where she strives to deepen her persona, making it more adult while still recognizably Britney. [...] It does sound like the work of a star who has now found and refined her voice, resulting in her best record yet."<sup id="cite_ref-britney-2001_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britney-2001-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The album was honored with two Grammy nominations‚ÄîBest Pop Vocal Album and Best Female Pop Vocal Performance for "<a href="/wiki/Overprotected" title="Overprotected">Overprotected</a>"‚Äî and was listed in 2008 as one of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s "100 Best Albums from the Past 25 Years".<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_a_Slave_4_U" title="I&#39;m a Slave 4 U">I'm a Slave 4 U</a>", became a top-ten hit worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Spears's performance of the single at the <a href="/wiki/2001_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2001 MTV Video Music Awards">2001 MTV Video Music Awards</a> featured a caged tiger and a large <a href="/wiki/Burmese_python" title="Burmese python">albino python</a> draped over her shoulders. It was harshly received by animal rights organization <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">PETA</a>, who claimed the animals were mistreated and scrapped plans for an anti-fur billboard that was to feature Spears.<sup id="cite_ref-vma_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vma-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Jocelyn Vena of MTV summarized Spears's performance at the ceremony, saying, "draping herself in a white python and slithering around a steamy garden setting ‚Äì surrounded by dancers in zebra and tiger outfits ‚Äì Spears created one of the most striking visuals in the 27-year history of the show."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>To support the album, Spears embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Dream_Within_a_Dream_Tour" title="Dream Within a Dream Tour">Dream Within a Dream Tour</a>. The show was critically praised for its technical innovations, the <i><a href="/wiki/Pi%C3%A8ce_de_r%C3%A9sistance" title="Pi√®ce de r√©sistance">pi√®ce de r√©sistance</a></i> being a water screen that pumped two tons of water into the stage.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The tour grossed $43.7&#160;million, becoming the second highest-grossing tour of 2002 by a female artist, behind <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Living_Proof:_The_Farewell_Tour" title="Living Proof: The Farewell Tour">Farewell Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Her career success was highlighted by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> in 2002, as Spears was ranked the world's most powerful celebrity.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Spears also landed her first starring role in <i><a href="/wiki/Crossroads_(2002_film)" title="Crossroads (2002 film)">Crossroads</a></i>, released in February 2002. Although the film was largely panned, critics praised Spears's acting and the film was a box office success.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cross_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cross-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <i>Crossroads</i>, which had a $12&#160;million budget, went on to gross over $61.1&#160;million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-cross_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cross-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2002, Spears opened her first restaurant, Nyla, in New York City, but terminated her relationship in November, citing mismanagement and "management's failure to keep her fully apprised".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In July 2002, Spears announced she would take a six-month break from her career; however, she went back into the studio in November to record her new album.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Spears's relationship with Justin Timberlake ended after three years. In December 2002, Timberlake released the song "<a href="/wiki/Cry_Me_a_River_(Justin_Timberlake_song)" title="Cry Me a River (Justin Timberlake song)">Cry Me a River</a>" as the second single from his <a href="/wiki/Justified_(album)" title="Justified (album)">solo debut album</a>. The music video featured a Spears look-alike and fueled the rumors that she had been unfaithful to him.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> As a response, Spears wrote the ballad "<a href="/wiki/Everytime" title="Everytime">Everytime</a>" with her backing vocalist and friend <a href="/wiki/Annet_Artani" title="Annet Artani">Annet Artani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The same year, <a href="/wiki/Limp_Bizkit" title="Limp Bizkit">Limp Bizkit</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Fred_Durst" title="Fred Durst">Fred Durst</a> said that he was in a relationship with Spears. However, Spears denied Durst's claims. In a 2009 interview, he explained that "I just guess at the time it was taboo for a guy like me to be associated with a gal like her."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2003.E2.80.932005:_In_the_Zone_and_marriages"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2003‚Äì2005:_In_the_Zone_and_marriages">2003‚Äì2005: <i>In the Zone</i> and marriages</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Britney_Spears.jpg/170px-Britney_Spears.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Britney_Spears.jpg/255px-Britney_Spears.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Britney_Spears.jpg/340px-Britney_Spears.jpg 2x" data-file-width="508" data-file-height="764" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spears performing at the NFL Kickoff Live in September 2003</div></div></div>
<p>In August 2003, Spears opened the <a href="/wiki/2003_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2003 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> with <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, performing "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin</a>". Halfway through they were joined by Madonna, with whom they both kissed. The incident was highly publicized.<sup id="cite_ref-cross_72-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cross-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In 2008, MTV listed the performance as the number-one opening moment in the history of MTV Video Music Awards,<sup id="cite_ref-openingvma_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-openingvma-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine cited it as one of the twenty-five sexiest music moments on television history.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Spears released her fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Zone" title="In the Zone">In the Zone</a></i>, in November 2003. She assumed more creative control by writing and co-producing most of the material.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> called it "A supremely confident dance record that also illustrates Spears's development as a songwriter."<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a> listed the album as one of "The 50 Most Important Recording of the Decade", adding that "the decade's history of impeccably crafted pop is written on her body of work."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <i>In the Zone</i> sold over 609,000 copies in the United States during its first week of availability in the United States, debuting at the top of the charts, making Spears the first female artist in the SoundScan era to have her first four studio albums to debut at number one.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It also debuted at the top of the charts in France and the top ten in Belgium, Denmark, Sweden and the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> <i>In the Zone</i> sold over 10 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The album produced four singles: "<a href="/wiki/Me_Against_the_Music" title="Me Against the Music">Me Against the Music</a>", a collaboration with Madonna; "<a href="/wiki/Toxic_(song)" title="Toxic (song)">Toxic</a>"‚Äîwhich won Spears her first Grammy for <a href="/wiki/Best_Dance_Recording" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Dance Recording">Best Dance Recording</a>; "<a href="/wiki/Everytime" title="Everytime">Everytime</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Outrageous_(song)" title="Outrageous (song)">Outrageous</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2004, Spears married childhood friend Jason Allen Alexander at <a href="/wiki/A_Little_White_Wedding_Chapel" title="A Little White Wedding Chapel">A Little White Wedding Chapel</a> in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a>. The marriage was <a href="/wiki/Annulment" title="Annulment">annulled</a> 55 hours later, following a petition to the court that stated that Spears "lacked understanding of her actions".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2004, she embarked on <a href="/wiki/The_Onyx_Hotel_Tour" title="The Onyx Hotel Tour">The Onyx Hotel Tour</a> in support of <i>In the Zone</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In June 2004, Spears fell and injured her left knee during the music video shoot for "<a href="/wiki/Outrageous_(song)" title="Outrageous (song)">Outrageous</a>". Spears underwent <a href="/wiki/Arthroscopy" title="Arthroscopy">arthroscopic surgery</a>. She was forced to remain six weeks with a thigh brace, followed by eight to twelve weeks of rehabilitation, which caused The Onyx Hotel Tour to be canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During 2004, Spears became involved in the <a href="/wiki/Kabbalah_Centre" title="Kabbalah Centre">Kabbalah Centre</a> through her friendship with <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kabbalah_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kabbalah-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2004, Spears became engaged to American dancer <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Federline" title="Kevin Federline">Kevin Federline</a>, whom she had met three months before. The romance received intense attention from the media, since Federline had recently broken up with actress <a href="/wiki/Shar_Jackson" title="Shar Jackson">Shar Jackson</a>, who was still pregnant with their second child at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The stages of their relationship were chronicled in Spears's first reality show <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_%26_Kevin:_Chaotic" class="mw-redirect" title="Britney &amp; Kevin: Chaotic">Britney &amp; Kevin: Chaotic</a></i>. They held a wedding ceremony on September 18, 2004, but were not legally married until three weeks later on October 6 due to a delay finalizing the couple's prenuptial agreement.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after, she released her first perfume with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Arden" title="Elizabeth Arden">Elizabeth Arden</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Curious_(fragrance)" title="Curious (fragrance)">Curious</a></i>, which broke the company's first-week gross for a perfume.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In October 2004, Spears took a career break to start a family.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits:_My_Prerogative" title="Greatest Hits: My Prerogative">Greatest Hits: My Prerogative</a></i>, her first greatest hits <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation album</a>, was released in November 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Spears's <a href="/wiki/Cover_version" title="Cover version">cover version</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Brown" title="Bobby Brown">Bobby Brown</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/My_Prerogative" title="My Prerogative">My Prerogative</a>" was released as the lead single from the album, reaching the top of the charts in Finland, Ireland, Italy and Norway.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Do_Somethin%27" title="Do Somethin&#39;">Do Somethin'</a>", was a top ten hit in Australia, the United Kingdom and other countries of mainland Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In August 2005, Spears released "<a href="/wiki/Someday_(I_Will_Understand)" title="Someday (I Will Understand)">Someday (I Will Understand)</a>", which was dedicated to her first child, a son, who was born the following month.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> In November 2005, she released her first remix compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/B_in_the_Mix:_The_Remixes" title="B in the Mix: The Remixes">B in the Mix: The Remixes</a></i>, which consists of eleven remixes.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> It has sold over 1 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2006.E2.80.932007:_Personal_struggles_and_Blackout"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2006‚Äì2007:_Personal_struggles_and_Blackout">2006‚Äì2007: Personal struggles and <i>Blackout</i></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="428" data-file-height="258" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_car_october_2007_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spears leaving court surrounded by press in October 2007</div></div></div>
<p>In February 2006, pictures surfaced of Spears driving with her son, Sean, on her lap instead of in a car seat. Child advocates were horrified by the photos of her holding the wheel with one hand and Sean with the other. Spears claimed that the situation happened because of a frightening encounter with paparazzi, and that it was a mistake on her part.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The following month, she <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest-starred</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Will_%26_Grace" title="Will &amp; Grace">Will &amp; Grace</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Buy,_Buy_Baby" title="Buy, Buy Baby">Buy, Buy Baby</a>" as closeted lesbian Amber Louise.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> She announced she no longer studied Kabbalah in June 2006, explaining, "my baby is my religion."<sup id="cite_ref-kabbalah_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kabbalah-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Two months later, Spears posed nude for the cover of <i><a href="/wiki/Harper%27s_Bazaar" title="Harper&#39;s Bazaar">Harper's Bazaar</a></i>. The picture was heavily compared to <a href="/wiki/Demi_Moore" title="Demi Moore">Demi Moore</a>'s <a href="/wiki/More_Demi_Moore" title="More Demi Moore">August 1991 <i>Vanity Fair</i> cover</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In September 2006, she gave birth to her second child, a son.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In November 2006, Spears filed for divorce from Federline, citing <a href="/wiki/Irreconcilable_differences" title="Irreconcilable differences">irreconcilable differences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Their divorce was finalized in July 2007, when the couple reached a global settlement and agreed to share joint custody of their children.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears's aunt Sandra Bridges Covington, with whom she had been very close, died of <a href="/wiki/Ovarian_cancer" title="Ovarian cancer">ovarian cancer</a> in January 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> In February, Spears stayed in a <a href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation" title="Drug rehabilitation">drug rehabilitation</a> facility in <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a> for less than a day. The following night, she shaved her head with electric clippers at a hair salon in <a href="/wiki/Tarzana,_Los_Angeles" title="Tarzana, Los Angeles">Tarzana, Los Angeles</a>. She admitted herself to other treatment facilities during the following weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In May 2007, she produced a series of promotional concerts at <a href="/wiki/House_of_Blues" title="House of Blues">House of Blues</a> venues, titled <a href="/wiki/The_M%2BM%27s_Tour" title="The M+M&#39;s Tour">The M+M's Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> In October 2007, Spears lost physical custody of her children to Federline. The reasons of the court ruling were not revealed to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Spears was also sued by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Vuitton" title="Louis Vuitton">Louis Vuitton</a> over her 2005 music video "Do Somethin'" for upholstering her <a href="/wiki/Hummer" title="Hummer">Hummer</a> interior in counterfeit Louis Vuitton cherry blossom fabric, which resulted in the video being banned on European TV stations.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2007, Spears released her fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blackout_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Blackout (Britney Spears album)">Blackout</a></i>. The album debuted at the top of charts in Canada and Ireland, number two in the U.S. <i>Billboard</i> 200, France, Japan, Mexico and the United Kingdom and the top ten in Australia, Korea, New Zealand and many European nations. In the United States, Spears became the only female artist to have her first five studio albums debut at the two top slots of the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The album received positive reviews from critics and has sold over 3 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> <i>Blackout</i> won Album of the Year at <a href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Europe Music Awards 2008">MTV Europe Music Awards 2008</a> and was listed as the fifth Best Pop Album of the Decade by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Spears performed the lead single "<a href="/wiki/Gimme_More" title="Gimme More">Gimme More</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2007 MTV Video Music Awards">2007 MTV Video Music Awards</a>. The performance was panned by many critics.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Despite the backlash, the single rocketed to worldwide success, peaking at number one in Canada and the top ten in almost every country it charted.<sup id="cite_ref-can_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-can-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ultratop2007_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ultratop2007-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The second single "<a href="/wiki/Piece_of_Me_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Piece of Me (Britney Spears song)">Piece of Me</a>" reached the top of the charts in Ireland and reached the top five in Australia, Canada, Denmark, New Zealand and the United Kingdom. The third single "<a href="/wiki/Break_the_Ice_(Britney_Spears_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Break the Ice (Britney Spears song)">Break the Ice</a>" was released the following year and had moderate success due to Spears not being able to promote it properly.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In December 2007, Spears began a relationship with <a href="/wiki/Paparazzo" class="mw-redirect" title="Paparazzo">paparazzo</a> Adnan Ghalib.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2008.E2.80.932010:_Conservatorship_and_Circus"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008‚Äì2010:_Conservatorship_and_Circus">2008‚Äì2010: Conservatorship and <i>Circus</i></span></h3>
<p>In January 2008, Spears refused to relinquish custody of her sons to Federline's representatives. She was hospitalized at <a href="/wiki/Cedars-Sinai_Medical_Center" title="Cedars-Sinai Medical Center">Cedars-Sinai Medical Center</a> after police that had arrived at her house noted she appeared to be under the influence of an unidentified substance. The following day, Spears's visitation rights were suspended at an emergency court hearing, and Federline was given sole physical and legal custody of the children. She was committed to the psychiatric ward of <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_UCLA_Medical_Center" title="Ronald Reagan UCLA Medical Center">Ronald Reagan UCLA Medical Center</a> and put on <a href="/wiki/5150_(involuntary_psychiatric_hold)" class="mw-redirect" title="5150 (involuntary psychiatric hold)">5150 involuntary psychiatric hold</a>. The court placed her under temporary, and later, permanent<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Conservatorship" title="Conservatorship">conservatorship</a> of her father James Spears and attorney Andrew Wallet, giving them complete control of her assets.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She was released five days later.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg/180px-Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="252" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg/270px-Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg/360px-Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2076" data-file-height="2905" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney-Spears_Boys.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spears performing "<a href="/wiki/Boys_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Boys (Britney Spears song)">Boys</a>" at <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a> on March 5, 2009</div></div></div>
<p>The following month, Spears guest-starred on the <i><a href="/wiki/How_I_Met_Your_Mother" title="How I Met Your Mother">How I Met Your Mother</a></i> episode "<a href="/wiki/Ten_Sessions" title="Ten Sessions">Ten Sessions</a>" as receptionist Abby. She received positive reviews for her performance, as well as bringing the series its highest ratings ever.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In July 2008, Spears regained some visitation rights after coming to an agreement with Federline and his counsel.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> In September 2008, Spears opened the <a href="/wiki/2008_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2008 MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> with a pre-taped comedy sketch with <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Hill" title="Jonah Hill">Jonah Hill</a> and an introduction speech. She won <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Female_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Female Video">Best Female Video</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Best_Pop_Video" title="MTV Video Music Award for Best Pop Video">Best Pop Video</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award_for_Video_of_the_Year" title="MTV Video Music Award for Video of the Year">Video of the Year</a> for "Piece of Me".<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> A 60-minute introspective documentary, <i><a href="/wiki/Britney:_For_the_Record" title="Britney: For the Record">Britney: For the Record</a></i>, was produced to chronicle Spears's return to the recording industry. Directed by Phil Griffin, <i>For the Record</i> was shot in <a href="/wiki/Beverly_Hills" class="mw-redirect" title="Beverly Hills">Beverly Hills</a>, Hollywood, and New York City during the third quarter of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The documentary was broadcast on MTV to 5.6&#160;million viewers for the two airings on the premiere night. It was the highest rating in its Sunday night timeslot and in the network's history.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2008, Spears's sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Circus_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Circus (Britney Spears album)">Circus</a></i> was released. It received positive reviews from critics<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> and debuted at number one in Canada, Czech Republic and the United States, and inside the top ten in many European nations.<sup id="cite_ref-ultratop2007_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ultratop2007-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-circus_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circus-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> In the United States, Spears became the youngest female artist to have five albums debut at number one, earning a place in <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> She also became the only act in the Soundscan era to have four albums debut with 500,000 or more copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-circus_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-circus-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The album was one of the fastest-selling albums of the year,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and has sold 4 million copies worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Its lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Womanizer_(song)" title="Womanizer (song)">Womanizer</a>", became Spears's first number one in the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 since "...Baby One More Time". The single also topped the charts in Belgium, Canada, Denmark, Finland, France, Norway and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> It was also nominated for a Grammy in the category of Best Dance Recording.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In January 2009, Spears and her father James obtained a restraining order against her former manager Sam Lutfi, ex-boyfriend Adnan Ghalib and attorney Jon Eardley ‚Äì all of whom, court documents claim, had been conspiring to gain control of Spears's affairs. The restraining order forbids Lutfi and Ghalib from contacting Spears or coming within 250 yards of her, her property or family members.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Spears embarked on <a href="/wiki/The_Circus_Starring_Britney_Spears" title="The Circus Starring Britney Spears">The Circus Starring Britney Spears</a> in March 2009. With a gross of U.S. $131.8&#160;million, it became the fifth highest-grossing tour of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2009, Spears released her second greatest hits album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Singles_Collection_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="The Singles Collection (Britney Spears album)">The Singles Collection</a></i>. The album's lead and only single, "<a href="/wiki/3_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="3 (Britney Spears song)">3</a>" became her third number one single in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In May 2010, Spears's representatives confirmed she was dating her agent Jason Trawick, and that they had decided to end their professional relationship to focus on their personal relationship.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Spears designed a limited edition clothing line for <a href="/wiki/Candie%27s" title="Candie&#39;s">Candie's</a>, which was released in stores in July 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Vena_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vena-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In September 2010, she made a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo appearance</a> on a Spears-themed tribute episode of American TV show <i><a href="/wiki/Glee_(TV_series)" title="Glee (TV series)">Glee</a></i>, titled "<a href="/wiki/Britney/Brittany" title="Britney/Brittany">Britney/Brittany</a>". The episode drew <i>Glee'</i>s highest ratings ever.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932012:_Femme_Fatale_and_The_X_Factor"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011‚Äì2012:_Femme_Fatale_and_The_X_Factor">2011‚Äì2012: <i>Femme Fatale</i> and <i>The X Factor</i></span></h3>
<p>In March 2011, Spears released her seventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Femme Fatale (Britney Spears album)">Femme Fatale</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The album peaked at number one in the United States, Canada, and Australia, and peaked inside the top ten on nearly every other chart. Its peak in the United States ties Britney with <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> for the third-most number ones among women.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard_472190_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard_472190-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It has sold 1 million copies in the United States, and has been certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">RIAA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FFT4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Image of a blond female performer surrounded by a group of dancers. She is sitting on a purple coach and wearing a golden outfit. The dancers are wearing short black hooded sweatshirts." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/FFT4.jpg/220px-FFT4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/FFT4.jpg/330px-FFT4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/FFT4.jpg/440px-FFT4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FFT4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spears performing at the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a>, July 2011</div></div></div>
<p>The album's lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Hold_It_Against_Me" title="Hold It Against Me">Hold It Against Me</a>" debuted at number-one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, becoming Spears's fourth number-one single on the chart and making her the second artist in history to have two consecutive singles debut at number one, after <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hiamrecord_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiamrecord-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The second single "<a href="/wiki/Till_the_World_Ends" title="Till the World Ends">Till the World Ends</a>" peaked at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 in May,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> while the third single "<a href="/wiki/I_Wanna_Go" title="I Wanna Go">I Wanna Go</a>" reached number seven in August. <i>Femme Fatale</i> became Spears's first album in which three of its songs reached the top ten of the chart. The fourth and final single "<a href="/wiki/Criminal_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Criminal (Britney Spears song)">Criminal</a>" was released in September 2011. The music video caused controversy when British politicians criticized Spears for using replica guns while filming the video in an area of London that had been badly affected by the <a href="/wiki/2011_England_riots" title="2011 England riots">2011 England riots</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Spears's management briefly responded, stating, "The video is a fantasy story featuring Britney's boyfriend, Jason Trawick, which literally plays out the lyrics of a song written three years before the riots ever happened."<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> In April 2011, Spears appeared in a remix of <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/S%26M_(song)" title="S&amp;M (song)">S&amp;M</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> It reached number one in the US later in the month, giving Spears her fifth number one on the chart.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> On <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s 2011 Year-End list, Spears was ranked number fourteen on the Artists of the Year,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> thirty-two on <i>Billboard</i> 200 artists and ten on <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 artists.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Spears co-wrote "<a href="/wiki/Whiplash_(Selena_Gomez_%26_the_Scene_song)" title="Whiplash (Selena Gomez &amp; the Scene song)">Whiplash</a>", a song from American pop rock band <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez_%26_the_Scene" title="Selena Gomez &amp; the Scene">Selena Gomez &amp; the Scene</a>' third album <i><a href="/wiki/When_the_Sun_Goes_Down_(Selena_Gomez_%26_the_Scene_album)" title="When the Sun Goes Down (Selena Gomez &amp; the Scene album)">When the Sun Goes Down</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2011, Spears embarked on the <a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_Tour" title="Femme Fatale Tour">Femme Fatale Tour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> The first ten dates of the tour grossed $6.2&#160;million, landing the fifty-fifth spot on Pollstar's Top 100 North American Tours list for the half-way point of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> The tour ended on December 10, 2011 in Puerto Rico after 79 performances.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> A DVD of the tour was released in November 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In August 2011, Spears received the <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson_Video_Vanguard_Award" title="Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award">Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The next month, she released her second remix album, <i><a href="/wiki/B_in_the_Mix:_The_Remixes_Vol._2" title="B in the Mix: The Remixes Vol. 2">B in the Mix: The Remixes Vol. 2</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> In December, Spears became engaged to her long-time boyfriend Jason Trawick, who had formerly been her agent.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Trawick became a co-conservator of Spears, alongside her father, in April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> In January 2013, Spears and Trawick ended their engagement. Trawick was also removed as Spears's co-conservator, restoring her father as the sole conservator.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2012, Spears was hired to replace <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Scherzinger" title="Nicole Scherzinger">Nicole Scherzinger</a> as a judge for the <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._season_2)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (U.S. season 2)">second season</a> of the <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (U.S. TV series)">U.S. version</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor" title="The X Factor">The X Factor</a></i>, joining <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>, <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">L.A. Reid</a> and fellow new judge <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a>, who replaced <a href="/wiki/Paula_Abdul" title="Paula Abdul">Paula Abdul</a>. With a reported salary of $15&#160;million, she became the highest-paid judge on a singing competition series in television history.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> broke her record in 2018 after Perry was signed for a $25-million salary to serve as a judge on <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>'s revival of <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> She mentored the Teens category; her final act, <a href="/wiki/Carly_Rose_Sonenclar" title="Carly Rose Sonenclar">Carly Rose Sonenclar</a>, was named the runner-up of the season. Spears did not return for the show's third season and her spot was filled by <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Rowland" title="Kelly Rowland">Kelly Rowland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Spears was featured on <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Scream_%26_Shout" title="Scream &amp; Shout">Scream &amp; Shout</a>", which was released as a single from his fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Willpower_(will.i.am_album)" title="Willpower (will.i.am album)">#willpower</a></i> (2013). The song later became Spears's sixth number one single on the UK Singles Chart and peaked at No. 3 on US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. Scream &amp; Shout was among the best selling songs of 2012 and 2013 with denoting sales of over 8.1&#160;million worldwide, the accompanying music video was the third-most viewed video in 2013 on <a href="/wiki/VEVO" class="mw-redirect" title="VEVO">VEVO</a> despite the video being released in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (January 2015)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In December, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine named her music's top-earning woman of 2012, with estimated earnings of $58&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013.E2.80.932015:_Britney_Jean_and_Britney:_Piece_of_Me"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013‚Äì2015:_Britney_Jean_and_Britney:_Piece_of_Me">2013‚Äì2015: <i>Britney Jean</i> and Britney: Piece of Me</span></h3>
<p>Spears began work on her eighth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_Jean" title="Britney Jean">Britney Jean</a></i>, in December 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> and enlisted <a href="/wiki/Will.i.am" title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a> as its executive producer in May 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> During the production of <i>Britney Jean</i>, Spears recorded the song "<a href="/wiki/Ooh_La_La_(Britney_Spears_song)" title="Ooh La La (Britney Spears song)">Ooh La La</a>" for the soundtrack of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Smurfs_2" title="The Smurfs 2">The Smurfs 2</a></i>, which was released in June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> On September 17, 2013, she appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> to announce her two-year concert residency at <a href="/wiki/Planet_Hollywood_Resort_%26_Casino" class="mw-redirect" title="Planet Hollywood Resort &amp; Casino">Planet Hollywood Resort &amp; Casino</a> in Las Vegas, titled <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a>. It began on December 27, 2013, and included a total of 100 shows throughout 2014 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> During the same appearance, Spears announced that <i>Britney Jean</i> would be released on December 3, 2013, in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> It was released through <a href="/wiki/RCA_Records" title="RCA Records">RCA Records</a> due to the disbandment of <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> in 2011, which had formed the joint <a href="/wiki/RCA/Jive_Label_Group" title="RCA/Jive Label Group">RCA/Jive Label Group</a> (initially known as BMG Label Group) between 2007 and 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <i>Britney Jean</i> became Spears's final project under her original recording contract with Jive, which had guaranteed the release of eight studio albums.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> The record received a low amount of promotion and had little commercial impact, reportedly due to time conflicts involving preparations for Britney: Piece of Me.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Upon its release, the record debuted at number four on the U.S. <i>Billboard</i> 200 with first-week sales of 107,000 copies, becoming her lowest-peaking and lowest-selling album in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <i>Britney Jean</i> debuted at number 34 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>, selling 12,959 copies in its first week. In doing so, it became Spears's lowest-charting and lowest-selling album in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BritneyPOM3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/BritneyPOM3.jpg/180px-BritneyPOM3.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/BritneyPOM3.jpg/270px-BritneyPOM3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/BritneyPOM3.jpg/360px-BritneyPOM3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1993" data-file-height="2855" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BritneyPOM3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spears performing during her Las Vegas concert residency, <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Britney: Piece of Me</a>, in January 2014</div></div></div>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Work_Bitch" title="Work Bitch">Work Bitch</a>" was released as the lead single from <i>Britney Jean</i> on September 16, 2013, one day earlier than expected after being <a href="/wiki/Internet_leak" title="Internet leak">leaked</a> online.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> It debuted and peaked at number 12 on the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> marking Spears's 31st song on the chart and the fifth highest debut of her career on the chart, and her seventh in the top 20. It also marked Spears's 19th top 20 hit and overall her 23rd top 40 hit. The song marked Spears's highest sales debut since her 2011 number one hit "<a href="/wiki/Hold_It_Against_Me" title="Hold It Against Me">Hold It Against Me</a>". "Work Bitch" also had commercial success in the UK debuting and peaking at number 7 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>. The song also charted well in several other countries, peaking within the top ten of the charts in Brazil, Canada, France, Italy, Mexico, Spain and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>
