2x" data-file-width="1682" data-file-height="2114" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:135px;max-width:135px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="Janet Jackson performing" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/133px-JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="133" height="169" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/200px-JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_%28cropped%29.jpg/266px-JanetJacksonUnbreakableTourSanFran2015_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1562" data-file-height="1984" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Spears has cited artists such as <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> (<i>left</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a> (<i>right</i>) as her major influences</div></div></div></div>
<p>Spears has cited her major influences in her career as being <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson" title="Janet Jackson">Janet Jackson</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, her "three favorite artists" as a child whom she would "sing along to [...] day and night in [her] living room"; Houston's "<a href="/wiki/I_Have_Nothing" title="I Have Nothing">I Have Nothing</a>" was the song she auditioned to that landed her record deal with Jive Records.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Throughout her career, Spears has drawn frequent comparisons to Madonna and Jackson in particular, in terms of vocals, choreography and stage presence. According to Spears: "I know when I was younger, I looked up to people... like, you know, Janet Jackson and Madonna. And they were major inspirations for me. But I also had my own identity and I knew who I was."<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> In the 2002 book <i>Madonnastyle</i> by Carol Clerk, she is quoted saying: "I have been a huge fan of Madonna since I was a little girl. She's the person that I've really looked up to. I would really, really like to be a legend like Madonna."<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After meeting Spears face to face, Janet Jackson stated: "she said to me, 'I'm such a big fan; I really admire you.' That's so flattering. Everyone gets inspiration from some place. And it's awesome to see someone else coming up who's dancing and singing, and seeing how all these kids relate to her. A lot of people put it down, but what she does is a positive thing."<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Madonna said of Spears in the documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Britney:_For_the_Record" title="Britney: For the Record">Britney: For the Record</a></i>: "I admire her talent as an artist [...] There are aspects about her that I recognize in myself when I first started out in my career".<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> She has also named <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otis_Redding" title="Otis Redding">Otis Redding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain" title="Shania Twain">Shania Twain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyonc√©">Beyonc√©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natalie_Imbruglia" title="Natalie Imbruglia">Natalie Imbruglia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prince_(musician)" title="Prince (musician)">Prince</a> as sources of inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-shane_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shane-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> Spears also felt inspired by artists from younger generations, such as <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ariana_Grande" title="Ariana Grande">Ariana Grande</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span></h3>
<p>Spears is described as a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> singer<sup id="cite_ref-bsbiography_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bsbiography-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and generally explores the genre in the form of <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShuker201299_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShuker201299-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAppellHemphill2006&quot;Dance_Pop&quot;_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAppellHemphill2006&quot;Dance_Pop&quot;-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jackson_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jackson-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup></span> Following her debut, she was credited with influencing the revival of <a href="/wiki/Teen_pop" title="Teen pop">teen pop</a> in the late 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-rsspears_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsspears-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Rob Sheffield of <i>Rolling Stone</i> wrote: "Spears carries on the classic archetype of the rock &amp; roll teen queen, the dungaree doll, the angel baby who just has to make a scene."<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> In a review for <i>...Baby One More Time</i>, Stephen Thomas Erlewine of AllMusic referred to her music as a "blend of infectious, rap-inflected dance-pop and smooth balladry."<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> <i>Oops!...I Did It Again</i> saw Spears working with several <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">contemporary R&amp;B</a> producers, which led to "a combination of bubblegum, urban soul, and <a href="/wiki/Raga" title="Raga">raga</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> Her third studio album, <i>Britney</i> derived from the teen pop niche "[r]hythmically and melodically", but was described as "sharper, tougher than what came before", incorporating genres such as R&amp;B, disco and funk.<sup id="cite_ref-britney-2001_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britney-2001-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NMEbritney_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMEbritney-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears has explored and heavily incorporated the genres of <a href="/wiki/Electropop" title="Electropop">electropop</a><sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ladailynews_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ladailynews-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance music</a> in her records, as well as influences of <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">urban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> which are most present in <i>In the Zone</i> and <i>Blackout</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-ladailynews_282-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ladailynews-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allmusicitz_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicitz-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allmusicblackout_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicblackout-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> <i>Femme Fatale</i> and <i>Britney Jean</i> were also heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> genres.<sup id="cite_ref-Allmusicff_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusicff-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardianbj_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianbj-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The music found on <i>...Baby One More Time</i> and <i>Oops!... I Did It Again</i> generally explores themes such as love and relationships from a teenager's point of view.<sup id="cite_ref-ewney2001_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ewney2001-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> After the enormous success of her first two studio albums, Spears's team and producers wanted to maintain the formula that took her to the top of the charts.<sup id="cite_ref-ewney2001_287-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ewney2001-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> Spears, however, was no longer satisfied with the sound and themes covered on her records. She cowrote five songs and choose each track's producer on <i>Britney</i>, her third studio album, which lyrics address the subjects of reaching adulthood, sexuality and self-discovery.<sup id="cite_ref-britney-2001_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britney-2001-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ewney2001_287-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ewney2001-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NMEbritney_280-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NMEbritney-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> Sex, dancing, freedom and love continued to be Spears's music main subjects on her subsequent albums.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicitz_283-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicitz-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-allmusicblackout_284-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicblackout-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardianbj_286-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardianbj-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Allmusicff_285-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusicff-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Her fifth studio album, <i>Blackout</i>, also address issues such as media scrutiny and fame, most notably in "Piece of Me".<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicblackout_284-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicblackout-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Voice">Voice</span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_You_Got_It_All.ogg" title="File:Britney Spears - You Got It All.ogg">"You Got It All"</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="28.424376417234" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Britney_Spears_-_You_Got_It_All.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/3b/Britney_Spears_-_You_Got_It_All.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (65 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="65270" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/3/3b/Britney_Spears_-_You_Got_It_All.ogg/Britney_Spears_-_You_Got_It_All.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="189336" /><track src="/w/api.php?action=timedtext&amp;title=File%3ABritney_Spears_-_You_Got_It_All.ogg&amp;lang=en&amp;trackformat=srt" kind="subtitles" type="text/x-srt" srclang="en" label="English (en) subtitles" data-dir="ltr" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The cover of <a href="/wiki/The_Jets_(Minnesota_band)" title="The Jets (Minnesota band)">The Jets</a>' song was the first song recorded by Spears for her then-label Jive in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> The prominent use of <a href="/wiki/Melisma" title="Melisma">melisma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vibrato" title="Vibrato">vibratos</a> as she continuously raises key into a high range was viewed as a <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a> influence.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup></div></div><hr /><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Freakshow.ogg" title="File:Britney Spears - Freakshow.ogg">"Freakshow"</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="20.489183673469" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Britney_Spears_-_Freakshow.ogg" data-mwprovider="local"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/d4/Britney_Spears_-_Freakshow.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (70 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="70240" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/transcoded/d/d4/Britney_Spears_-_Freakshow.ogg/Britney_Spears_-_Freakshow.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="196112" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The track is built around the 'wobbler' effect of <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a>, and her vocals are pitched down low, making her sound masculine.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> She was credited as one of the artists who prompted the genre within a pop mainstream audience.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup></div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table><p> Spears is a <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SopranoToBass_295-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SopranoToBass-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-billboardvmas_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboardvmas-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> Prior to her breakthrough success, she is described as having sung "much deeper than her highly recognizable trademark voice of today", with Eric Foster White, who worked with Spears for her debut album <i><a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)" title="...Baby One More Time (album)">...Baby One More Time</a></i>, being cited as "[shaping] her voice over the course of a month" upon being signed to <a href="/wiki/Jive_Records" title="Jive Records">Jive Records</a> "to where it is today‚Äîdistinctively, unmistakably Britney".<sup id="cite_ref-hughes145_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hughes145-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Rami Yacoub who co-produced Spears's debut album with lyricist Max Martin, commented, "I know from <a href="/wiki/Denniz_Pop" title="Denniz Pop">Denniz Pop</a> and Max's previous productions, when we do songs, there's kind of a nasal thing. With N' Sync and the Backstreet Boys, we had to push for that mid-nasal voice. When Britney did that, she got this kind of raspy, sexy voice."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Guy Blackman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Age" title="The Age">The Age</a></i> wrote that "[t]he thing about Spears, though, is that her biggest songs, no matter how committee-created or impossibly polished, have always been convincing because of her delivery, her commitment and her presence. [...] Spears expresses perfectly the conflicting urges of adolescence, the tension between chastity and sexual experience, between hedonism and responsibility, between confidence and vulnerability."<sup id="cite_ref-The_Age_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Age-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> Producer <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a>, who collaborated with Spears on her album <i><a href="/wiki/Britney_Jean" title="Britney Jean">Britney Jean</a></i>, stated regarding her vocals: "[Britney] didn't get so big just because [she] put on great shows; [she] got to be that way because [her voice is] unique: you hear two words and you know who is singing".<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears has also been criticized for her reliance on auto-tune<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> and her vocals being "over-processed" on records.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> Erlewine criticized Spears's poor singing abilities in a review for <i>Blackout</i>, saying, "Never the greatest vocalist, her thin squawk could be dismissed early in her career as an adolescent learning the ropes, but nearly a decade later her singing hasn't gotten any better, even if the studio tools to masquerade her weaknesses have."<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicblackout_284-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicblackout-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Joan Anderman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> remarked that "Spears sounds robotic, nearly inhuman, on her records, so processed is her voice by digital pitch-shifters and synthesizers."<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Michigan_Daily" title="The Michigan Daily">The Michigan Daily</a>'</i>s Kayla Upadhyaya provided a different point of view, saying, "Auto-tuned and over-processed vocals define Britney's voice as an artist, and in her music, auto-tune isn't so much a gimmick as it is an instrument used to highlight, contort and make a statement."<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage_performances">Stage performances</span></h3>
<p>Spears is known for her performances and its elaborated dance routines, which incorporates "belly-dancing and tempered erotic moves" that was credited for influencing "dance-heavy acts" such as <a href="/wiki/Danity_Kane" title="Danity Kane">Danity Kane</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Pussycat_Dolls" title="The Pussycat Dolls">the Pussycat Dolls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-abad1_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abad1-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vogueus_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogueus-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine readers voted Spears as the second Favorite Dancing Musician.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> Spears is described as being much more shy than what her stage persona suggests.<sup id="cite_ref-vicemb_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vicemb-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> She claimed that performing is "a boost to [her] confidence. It's like an alter-ego type thing. Something clicks and I go and turn into this different person. I think it's kind of a gift to be able to do that."<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> Her 2000, 2001, and 2003 MTV Video Music Awards performances received praise,<sup id="cite_ref-timevmas_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timevmas-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> while her 2007 presentation was widely panned by critics, as she "teetered through her dance steps and mouthed only occasional words".<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> <i>Billboard</i> called her 2016 "comeback" performance at the show "An effective, but not entirely glorious, bid to regain pop superstardom".<sup id="cite_ref-billboardvmas_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboardvmas-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After her knee injuries and personal struggles, Spears's "showmanship" and dance abilities came under criticism.<sup id="cite_ref-abad1_305-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-abad1-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lasvegas2017_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lasvegas2017-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Serge F. Kovaleski of <i>The New York Times</i> watched her <a href="/wiki/Britney:_Piece_of_Me" title="Britney: Piece of Me">Las Vegas concert residency</a> in 2016 and said: "Once a fluid, natural dancer, Ms. Spears can appear stiff, even robotic, today, relying on flailing arms and flashy sets."<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Sun" title="Las Vegas Sun">Las Vegas Sun</a>'</i>s <a href="/wiki/Robin_Leach" title="Robin Leach">Robin Leach</a> seemed more impressed over Spears's efforts on the concert by saying that she delivered a "flawless performance" on the residency's opening night.<sup id="cite_ref-leach_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leach-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It has been widely reported that Spears lip-syncs during live performances,<sup id="cite_ref-vogueus_306-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vogueus-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nmelevine_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmelevine-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> which often draws criticism from music critics and concert goers.<sup id="cite_ref-lasvegas2017_314-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lasvegas2017-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup> Some, however, claimed that, although she "got plenty of digital support", she "doesn't merely lip-sync" during her live shows.<sup id="cite_ref-spin_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spin-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Sabrina Weiss of <i><a href="/wiki/Refinery29" title="Refinery29">Refinery29</a></i> referred to her lip-syncing as a "well-known fact that's not even taboo anymore."<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> Noting on the prevalence of lip-syncing, <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Daily_News" title="Los Angeles Daily News">Los Angeles Daily News</a></i> opined: "In the context of a Britney Spears concert, does it really matter? [...] you [just] go for the somewhat-ridiculous spectacle of it all".<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> Spears spoke on the topic saying "[...] Because I'm dancing so much, I do have a little bit of playback, but there's a mixture of my voice and the playback." She added: "It really pisses me off because I'm busting my ass out there and singing at the same time and nobody ever gives me credit for it, you know?"<sup id="cite_ref-nmelevine_317-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nmelevine-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<p>Spears rose to fame as a <a href="/wiki/Bubblegum_pop" title="Bubblegum pop">bubblegum pop</a> singer in the late 1990s and was labelled as a <a href="/wiki/Teen_idol" title="Teen idol">teen idol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-vh130_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vh130-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine described Spears in her early years of fame as "the latest model of a classic product: the unneurotic pop star who performs her duties with <a href="/wiki/Vaudeville" title="Vaudeville">vaudevillian</a> pluck and spokesmodel charm."<sup id="cite_ref-stone99_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stone99-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> The April 1999 cover of <i>Rolling Stone</i> featured Spears lying on her bed, wearing an open top revealing her bra, and shorts.<sup id="cite_ref-stone99_326-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stone99-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/American_Family_Association" title="American Family Association">American Family Association</a> (AFA) referred to the shoot as "a disturbing mix of childhood innocence and adult sexuality" and called on "God-loving Americans to boycott stores selling Britney's albums." Spears responded to the outcry commenting, "What's the big deal? I have strong morals. [...] I'd do it again. I thought the pictures were fine. And I was tired of being compared to <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Gibson" title="Debbie Gibson">Debbie Gibson</a> and all of this bubblegum pop all the time."<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup> Shortly before, Spears had announced publicly she would remain a virgin until marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-biographybillboard_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biographybillboard-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg/170px-Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg/255px-Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg/340px-Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="730" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_-_Madame_Tussauds_London.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wax statue of Spears at <a href="/wiki/Madame_Tussauds" title="Madame Tussauds">Madame Tussauds</a> in London</div></div></div>
<p><i>Billboard</i> opined that, by the time she released her second album <i>Oops!... I Did it Again</i>, "There was a shift occurring in both the music and her public image: She was sharper, sexier and singing about more grown-up fare, setting the stage for 2001‚Äôs <i>Britney</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-billboard2016_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2016-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> <i>Britney'</i>s lead single "I'm a Slave 4 U" and its video were also credited for distancing her from her "wholesome bubblegum star" image of the past.<sup id="cite_ref-vh130_324-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vh130-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytimes2001_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes2001-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup> Stephen Thomas Erlewine of AllMusic commented, "If 2001's <i>Britney</i> was a transitional album, capturing Spears at the point when she <a href="/wiki/I%27m_Not_a_Girl,_Not_Yet_a_Woman" title="I&#39;m Not a Girl, Not Yet a Woman">wasn't a girl and not yet a woman</a>, its 2003 follow-up, <i>In the Zone</i>, is where she has finally completed that journey and turned into Britney, the Adult Woman." Erlewine compared Spears to her peer Christina Aguilera, explaining that both equated "maturity with transparent sexuality and the pounding sounds of nightclubs".<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicitz_283-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicitz-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears's erratic behavior and personal struggles during 2006‚Äî2008 were highly publicised<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> and affected both her career and public image.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicblackout_284-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicblackout-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tragedyrs_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tragedyrs-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> Erlewine reflected on that time of her career by saying that "each new disaster [was] stripping away any residual sexiness in her public image".<sup id="cite_ref-allmusicblackout_284-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusicblackout-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Spears later received favorable media attention. <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a>'</i>s Cady Lang observed that she looked healthier during her appearance at the 2008 MTV Video Music Awards,<sup id="cite_ref-timevmas_312-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timevmas-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Business_Insider" title="Business Insider">Business Insider</a></i> wrote an article about how Spears "lost control of her life [...] and then made an incredible career comeback".<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2002, she was ranked eight on <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 100 Sexiest Artists list,<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> and, in December 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Complex_(magazine)" title="Complex (magazine)">Complex</a></i> ranked her 12 on its 100 Hottest Female Singers of All Time list.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> Spears commented on her sex symbol image by saying, "[...] When I'm on stage, that's my time to do my thing and go there and be that ‚Äî and it's fun. It's exhilarating just to be something that you're not. And people tend to believe it."<sup id="cite_ref-ewney2001_287-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ewney2001-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, <i><a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)">People</a></i> cited her as one of the 50 Most Beautiful People.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears is also recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Gay_icon" title="Gay icon">gay icon</a>. She was honored with the 2018 <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Vanguard_Award" title="GLAAD Vanguard Award">GLAAD Vanguard Award</a> at the <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Media_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="GLAAD Media Awards">GLAAD Media Awards</a> for her role in "accelerating acceptance for the LGBTQ community".<sup id="cite_ref-spearsglaad_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spearsglaad-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <i>Billboard'</i>s Patrick Crowley reflected on her winning the award, "While it's no secret that LGBTQ fans saw their struggle reflected in Spears' particularly rough mid-career slump, followed by her phoenix-like rise back to the top of the charts‚Äîit's really her outstanding advocacy for the community that earned her this award."<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup> Manuel Betancourt of <i><a href="/wiki/Vice_(magazine)" title="Vice (magazine)">Vice</a></i> magazine wrote about the "queer adoration", especially of gay men, on Spears, and said that "Where other gay icons exude self-possession, Spears's fragile resilience has made her an even more fascinating role model, closer to <a href="/wiki/Judy_Garland" title="Judy Garland">Judy Garland</a> than to Lady Gaga [...] she's a glittering mirror ball, a fractured reflection of those men on the dance floor back onto themselves."<sup id="cite_ref-vicemb_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vicemb-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since her early years of stardom, Spears become a <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_journalism" title="Tabloid journalism">tabloid</a> fixture and a paparazzi target, which affected her personal life as well.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard2016_329-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2016-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-riseandfall_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riseandfall-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-biographybillboard_328-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biographybillboard-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> Steve Huey of AllMusic claimed that "among female singers of [Spears's] era [...] her celebrity star power was rivaled only by <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-biographybillboard_328-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-biographybillboard-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> 'Britney Spears' was <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>'s most popular search term between 2005 and 2008, and has been in a total of seven different years.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">&#91;339&#93;</a></sup> Spears was named as Most Searched Person in the <i>Guinness World Records</i> book edition 2007 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">&#91;340&#93;</a></sup> She was later named as the most searched person of the decade 2000‚Äì2009.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">&#91;341&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/E!#E!_Online" title="E!">E!</a>'</i>s Melanie Bromley described her 2007 highly publicised breakdown as "one of the biggest public meltdowns in pop culture history."<sup id="cite_ref-riseandfall_338-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-riseandfall-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> She reflected on that time of her life in a 2017 interview, saying "I think I had to give myself more breaks through my career and take responsibility for my mental health. [...] I wrote back then, that I was lost and didn't know what to do with myself. I was trying to please everyone around me because that who I am deep inside. There are moments where I look back and think: 'What the hell was I thinking?'"<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">&#91;342&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg/220px-Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg/330px-Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg/440px-Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britney_Spears_Hollywood_Star.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Spears's star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a></div></div></div>
<p>Spears was described by <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine as "One of the most controversial and successful female vocalists of the 2000s", which also pointed out that she, alongside other acts, "spearheaded the rise of post-millennial teen pop."<sup id="cite_ref-rsspears_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsspears-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup> Barbara Ellen of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> wrote in 2000: "Spears is famously one of the 'oldest' teenagers pop has ever produced, almost middle aged in terms of focus and determination. Many 19-year-olds haven't even started working by that age, whereas Britney, a former Mouseketeer, was that most unusual and volatile of American phenomena&#160;‚Äî a child with a full-time career. [...] Whereas other children develop at their own pace, Britney was developing at a pace set by the ferociously competitive American entertainment industry."<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">&#91;343&#93;</a></sup> <i>Billboard'</i>s Robert Kelly observed that Spears's "sexy and coy" vocals on her debut single "...Baby One More Time" "kicked off a new era of pop vocal stylings that would influence countless artists to come."<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">&#91;344&#93;</a></sup> Spears has been recognised with a number of <a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">honorific nicknames</a>, most notably the "Princess of Pop."<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">&#91;345&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">&#91;346&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Billboard</i> claimed that she "has earned her title as one of pop's reigning queens. Since her early days as a Mouseketeer, [Spears] has pushed the boundaries of 21st century sounds, paving the way for a generation of artists to shamelessly embrace glossy pop and redefine how one can accrue consistent success in the music industry."<sup id="cite_ref-billboard2016_329-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2016-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, she was ranked as the fourth <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 50 Greatest Women of the Video Era show list.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">&#91;347&#93;</a></sup> VH1 also cited her among its choices on the 100 Greatest Women in Music in 2012<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">&#91;348&#93;</a></sup> and the 200 Greatest Pop Culture Icons in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">&#91;349&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> critics ranked her single "Toxic" at number 92 on the 500 Greatest Songs of All Time list, writing that the song "reinvented popular dance music."<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">&#91;350&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>In 2011, Adam Markovitz of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> commented on Spears's voice and music: "We don't ask a whole lot from Britney Spears as an entertainer [...] we'll still send her straight up the charts simply because she's Britney. [...] She's an American institution, as deeply sacred and messed up as pro wrestling or the filibuster. [...] Spears is no technical singer, that's for sure. But backed by Martin and Dr. Luke's wall of pound, her vocals melt into a mix of babytalk coo and coital panting that is, in its own overprocessed way, just as iconic and propulsive as <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s yips or <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>'s snarls."<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">&#91;351&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2018, <i>Rolling Stone</i> included Spears on its Millennial 100 list and said that, following the release of her music career in the late 1990s, she "quickly became the princess of pop, helping to usher in a new era for the genre that had gone dormant in the decade that followed <a href="/wiki/New_Kids_on_the_Block" title="New Kids on the Block">New Kids on the Block</a>. [...] Spears would lead an army of pop stars... built on slick Max Martin productions, plenty of sexual innuendo and dance-heavy performances. [She became] one of the most successful artists of all time ‚Äî and a cautionary tale for a generation, whether they paid attention or not."<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">&#91;352&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears's work has influenced artists including <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">&#91;353&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-younginf_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-younginf-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Trainor" title="Meghan Trainor">Meghan Trainor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">&#91;355&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-younginf_354-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-younginf-354">&#91;354&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Key" title="Kelly Key">Kelly Key</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">&#91;356&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kristinia_DeBarge" title="Kristinia DeBarge">Kristinia DeBarge</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">&#91;357&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Little_Boots" title="Little Boots">Little Boots</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">&#91;358&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charli_XCX" title="Charli XCX">Charli XCX</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">&#91;359&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marina_and_the_Diamonds" class="mw-redirect" title="Marina and the Diamonds">Marina</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-360">&#91;360&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tegan_and_Sara" title="Tegan and Sara">Tegan and Sara</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">&#91;361&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pixie_Lott" title="Pixie Lott">Pixie Lott</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">&#91;362&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Grimes_(musician)" title="Grimes (musician)">Grimes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-grimes_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grimes-363">&#91;363&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">&#91;364&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hailee_Steinfeld" title="Hailee Steinfeld">Hailee Steinfeld</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">&#91;365&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tinashe" title="Tinashe">Tinashe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">&#91;366&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Justice" title="Victoria Justice">Victoria Justice</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">&#91;367&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cassie_Ventura" title="Cassie Ventura">Cassie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">&#91;368&#93;</a></sup> Leah Wellbaum of <a href="/wiki/Slothrust" title="Slothrust">Slothrust</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">&#91;369&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Saturdays" title="The Saturdays">The Saturdays</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">&#91;370&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Normani" title="Normani">Normani</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-371">&#91;371&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-372">&#91;372&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_(singer)" title="Cheryl (singer)">Cheryl</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">&#91;373&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lana_Del_Rey" title="Lana Del Rey">Lana Del Rey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">&#91;374&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Ava_Max" title="Ava Max">Ava Max</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">&#91;375&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/2011_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="2011 MTV Video Music Awards">2011 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> said that Spears "taught us all how to be fearless, and the industry wouldn't be the same without her."<sup id="cite_ref-vanguard_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vanguard-376">&#91;376&#93;</a></sup> Gaga has also cited Spears as an influence, calling her "the most provocative performer of my time."<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">&#91;377&#93;</a></sup> Before Spears joined <i>The X Factor</i>, <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a> explained that he is "fascinated by [Britney]. The fact that she's one of the most talked about ‚Äì not just pop stars ‚Äì but people in the world today, means that you've got this star power. [...] She's still hot, she's still having hit records and she's still controversial, there's a reason for that."<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">&#91;378&#93;</a></sup> Marina named Spears as the main influence behind her album <i><a href="/wiki/Electra_Heart" title="Electra Heart">Electra Heart</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">&#91;379&#93;</a></sup> Lana Del Rey has said that the music video for "Toxic" inspires her.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">&#91;380&#93;</a></sup> Spears has had a direct influence on singer <a href="/wiki/Porcelain_Black" title="Porcelain Black">Porcelain Black</a>'s work after growing up around her music as a child. Black describes her music as a "love child between" <a href="/wiki/Marilyn_Manson" title="Marilyn Manson">Marilyn Manson</a> and Spears.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">&#91;381&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears's much-publicized personal struggles and her career comeback after this period has inspired some artists. <a href="/wiki/Gwyneth_Paltrow" title="Gwyneth Paltrow">Gwyneth Paltrow</a>'s character in 2010 drama film <i><a href="/wiki/Country_Strong" title="Country Strong">Country Strong</a></i> was inspired by the singer's treatment by the media. According to film director Shana Fest, "that's where this movie came from. I mean, I was seeing what was happening in the media to Britney Spears. I think it's tragic how we treat people who give us so much, and we love to see them knocked down to build them back up again, to knock them down again."<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">&#91;382&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> has cited Spears's comeback after her much-publicized personal issues as an inspiration.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">&#91;383&#93;</a></sup> Spears's hounding by paparazzi and personal struggles also contributed to inspiring <a href="/wiki/Barry_Manilow" title="Barry Manilow">Barry Manilow</a>'s album <i><a href="/wiki/15_Minutes_(Barry_Manilow_album)" title="15 Minutes (Barry Manilow album)">15 Minutes</a></i>. Manilow said: "She couldn't have a life without them pulling up next to her car and following her and driving her crazy to the point where, that was around the time she shaved off her hair. [...] We all looked at it in horror [...] So it seemed like a thing to be writing an album about."<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">&#91;384&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bebo_Norman" title="Bebo Norman">Bebo Norman</a> wrote a song about Spears, called "<a href="/wiki/Britney_(Bebo_Norman_song)" title="Britney (Bebo Norman song)">Britney</a>", which was inspired by "culture's make-or-break treatment of celebrities."<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">&#91;385&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Achievements">Achievements</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Britney_Spears" title="List of awards and nominations received by Britney Spears">List of awards and nominations received by Britney Spears</a></div>
<p>Spears has earned numerous awards and accolades, including a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>; seven <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>; six <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson_Video_Vanguard_Award" title="Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award">Michael Jackson Video Vanguard Award</a>; seven <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Music Awards">Billboard Music Awards</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards#Millennium_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard Music Awards">Millennium Award</a>; the inaugural Radio Disney Icon Award; the <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Media_Award" title="GLAAD Media Award">GLAAD Media Award</a>'s <a href="/wiki/GLAAD_Vanguard_Award" title="GLAAD Vanguard Award">Vanguard Award</a> and a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>.
</p><p>She is listed by the <i><a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a></i> as having the "Best-selling album by a teenage solo artist" for her debut album <i>...Baby One More Time</i> which sold over thirteen million copies in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-386">&#91;386&#93;</a></sup> Melissa Ruggieri of the <i><a href="/wiki/Richmond_Times-Dispatch" title="Richmond Times-Dispatch">Richmond Times-Dispatch</a></i> reported: "She's also marked for being the best-selling teenage artist. Before she turned 20 in 2001, Spears sold more than 37 million albums worldwide".<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">&#91;387&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Britney_Spears&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, according to <i>Billboard</i>, she has sold 150 million records worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-billboard150_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard150-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> making her one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">best-selling music artists</a> of all time; and more than 70 million records in United States, including 36.9 million digital singles and 33.6 million digital albums.<sup id="cite_ref-usrecordsales_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usrecordsales-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-records_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-records-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Spears is also recognized as the best-selling female albums artist of the 2000s in the United States, as well as the fifth overall.<sup id="cite_ref-21sells_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21sells-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In December 2009, <i>Billboard</i> magazine ranked Spears the 8th Artist of the 2000s decade in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-bbad_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbad-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> She is one of the few artists in history to have had a number one single and a number one studio album in the US during each of the three decades of her career.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">&#91;388&#93;</a></sup> With "3" in 2009 and "Hold It Against Me" in 2011, she became the second artist after Mariah Carey in the Hot 100's history to debut at number one with two or more songs.<sup id="cite_ref-hiamrecord_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiamrecord-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Spears ranked at number twenty on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Greatest Of All Time Top <a href="/wiki/Dance_Club_Songs" title="Dance Club Songs">Dance Club</a> Artists list.<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">&#91;389&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Product_and_endorsements">Product and endorsements</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears_products" title="Britney Spears products">Britney Spears products</a></div>
<p>In 2000, the singer released a limited edition of sunglasses titled <i>Shades of Britney</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">&#91;390&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, Spears signed a deal with shoe company <a href="/wiki/Skechers" title="Skechers">Skechers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-391">&#91;391&#93;</a></sup> and a $7‚Äì8&#160;million promotional deal with <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>, their biggest entertainment deal at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">&#91;392&#93;</a></sup> Aside from numerous commercials with the latter during that year, she also appeared in a 2004 Pepsi television commercial in the theme of "Gladiators" with singers <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyonc√©">Beyonc√©</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pink_(singer)" title="Pink (singer)">Pink</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Iglesias" title="Enrique Iglesias">Enrique Iglesias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">&#91;393&#93;</a></sup> On June 19, 2002, she released her first multi-platform video game, <i>Britney's Dance Beat</i>, which received positive reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">&#91;394&#93;</a></sup> In March 2009, Spears was announced as the new face of clothing brand <i><a href="/wiki/Candie%27s" title="Candie&#39;s">Candie's</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-candy_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-candy-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> Dari Marder, chief marketing officer for the brand, explained why they choose the singer, saying, "everybody loves a comeback and nobody's doing it better than Britney. She's just poised for even greater success."<sup id="cite_ref-candy_395-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-candy-395">&#91;395&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Spears designed a limited edition line for the brand, which was released in stores in July 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Vena_139-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vena-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, she teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>, Make Up For Ever and <a href="/wiki/PlentyofFish" class="mw-redirect" title="PlentyofFish">PlentyofFish</a> to release her music video for "Hold It Against Me", earning her $500,000 for the product placement.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">&#91;396&#93;</a></sup> Spears also teamed up with <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a> in 2012 to release an exclusive version of <a href="/wiki/Twister_(game)" title="Twister (game)">Twister Dance</a>, which includes a remix of "Till the World Ends". The singer was also featured on a commercial, which was directed by <a href="/wiki/Ray_Kay" title="Ray Kay">Ray Kay</a>, to promote the game. Spears was also featured on the commercial of "Twister Rave" and the game included a Twister remix of "<a href="/wiki/Circus_(song)" title="Circus (song)">Circus</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">&#91;397&#93;</a></sup> In March 2018, it was revealed that Spears would be the face of <a href="/wiki/Kenzo_(brand)" title="Kenzo (brand)">KENZO</a>, a contemporary French luxury clothing house.<sup id="cite_ref-harpersbazaar.com.au_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harpersbazaar.com.au-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Spears's range of commercial deals and products also includes beauty care products and perfumes. She released her first perfume with <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Arden" title="Elizabeth Arden">Elizabeth Arden</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Curious_(fragrance)" title="Curious (fragrance)">Curious</a></i> in 2004, which broke the company's first-week gross for a perfume.<sup id="cite_ref-foxnews_25-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foxnews-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> By 2009, she had released seven more perfumes including Fantasy.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">&#91;398&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">&#91;399&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Spears released her eighth fragrance, <i><a href="/wiki/Radiance_(fragrance)" title="Radiance (fragrance)">Radiance</a></i>. In March 2011, company Brand Sense filed a lawsuit against Spears and Elizabeth Arden seeking $10&#160;million in damages, claiming that the singer and her father, Jamie, stopped paying their thirty-five percent commission that was agreed as part of the contract terms.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">&#91;400&#93;</a></sup> In July 2011, a Los Angeles judge denied the request by the company lawyers, claiming the fact that Spears is still under conservatorship.<sup id="cite_ref-radar1_401-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radar1-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> Brand Sense, however, stated that they would appeal the decision.<sup id="cite_ref-radar1_401-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-radar1-401">&#91;401&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, <i>Radiance</i> was re-issued as a new perfume titled <i>Cosmic Radiance</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">&#91;402&#93;</a></sup> Worldwide, Spears sold over one million bottles in the first five years, with gross receipts of $1.5&#160;billion. In 2016, Spears contacted <a href="/wiki/Glu_Mobile" title="Glu Mobile">Glu Mobile</a> to create her own role-playing game, <i>Britney Spears: American Dream</i>. The app officially launched in May 2016 and is compatible with <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">IOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> On June 17, 2016, Spears announced the release of her twentieth fragrance, <i>Private Show</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">&#91;403&#93;</a></sup> As of January&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Britney_Spears&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Spears has released 24 fragrances through Elizabeth Arden.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">&#91;404&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span></h3>
<p>The singer founded The Britney Spears Foundation, a charitable entity set up to help children in need. The philosophy behind the Foundation was that music and entertainment has a healing quality that can benefit children.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">&#91;405&#93;</a></sup> The Foundation also supported the annual Britney Spears Camp for the Performing Arts, where campers had the opportunity to explore and develop their talents.<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">&#91;406&#93;</a></sup> In April 2002, through the efforts of Spears and The Britney Spears Foundation, a grant of $1&#160;million was made to the Twin Towers Fund to support the children of uniformed service heroes affected by the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">terrorist attacks</a> of September 11, 2001, including New York City Fire Department and its Emergency Medical Services Command, the New York City Police Department, the Port Authority of New York and New Jersey, the New York State Office of court Administration and other government offices.<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">&#91;407&#93;</a></sup> However, it was reported in 2008 that the Foundation had a deficit of $200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">&#91;408&#93;</a></sup> After the singer went through conservatorship, her father and lawyer Andrew Wallet zeroed out the effort, leading to its closure in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">&#91;409&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 30, 2001, Spears, alongside <a href="/wiki/Bono" title="Bono">Bono</a> and other popular recording artists under the name "Artists Against AIDS Worldwide", released a single titled "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_Going_On_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="What&#39;s Going On (song)">What's Going On</a>", with the intention to benefit AIDS programs in Africa and other impoverished regions.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">&#91;410&#93;</a></sup> In the wake of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> in 2006, Spears donated $350,000 to <a href="/wiki/Music_Rising" title="Music Rising">Music Rising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lts_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lts-411">&#91;411&#93;</a></sup> Later in 2011, the singer raised $200,000 during An Evening of Southern Style at a private residence in Beverly Hills to benefit the <a href="/wiki/St._Bernard_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Bernard Project">St. Bernard Project</a>, with the help of several celebrities, including <a href="/wiki/Hilary_Duff" title="Hilary Duff">Hilary Duff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Selena_Gomez" title="Selena Gomez">Selena Gomez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Osbourne" title="Kelly Osbourne">Kelly Osbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kellan_Lutz" title="Kellan Lutz">Kellan Lutz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Kardashian" title="Kim Kardashian">Kim Kardashian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">&#91;412&#93;</a></sup> Spears has also helped several charities during her career, including Madonna's Kabbalah-based Spirituality for Kids,<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">&#91;413&#93;</a></sup> cancer charity Gilda's Club Worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">&#91;414&#93;</a></sup> Promises Foundation, and <a href="/wiki/United_Way_of_America" title="United Way of America">United Way</a>, with the latter two focused on giving families from various disadvantaged situations new hope and stable foundations for the future.<sup id="cite_ref-lts_411-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lts-411">&#91;411&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 24, 2015, Spears donated $120,000 to the Nevada Childhood Cancer Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">&#91;415&#93;</a></sup> In addition, $1 of each ticket sale for her Las Vegas residency, <i>Britney: Piece of Me</i>, was donated to the nonprofit organization.<sup id="cite_ref-416" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-416">&#91;416&#93;</a></sup> Spears also fundraised for the charity through social media, in addition to selling limited edition merchandise, with all proceeds going to the NCCF.<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">&#91;417&#93;</a></sup> On October 27, 2016, Spears partnered with <a href="/wiki/Zappos" title="Zappos">Zappos</a> and XCYCLE to host the <i>Britney Spears Piece of Me Charity Ride</i> in Boca Park, Las Vegas to raise additional money toward her goal of $1&#160;million for the NCCF, with $450,000 having already been raised from Spears's ticket sales and merchandise.<sup id="cite_ref-418" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-418">&#91;418&#93;</a></sup> Participants were entered for a chance to win a spin class with Spears herself. The event ultimately went on to raise $553,130.<sup id="cite_ref-419" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-419">&#91;419&#93;</a></sup> The fundraising ultimately led to the development of the NCCF Britney Spears Campus in Las Vegas, which saw its grand opening on November 4, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">&#91;420&#93;</a></sup> Spears also regularly participates in <a href="/wiki/Spirit_Day" title="Spirit Day">Spirit Day</a> to combat bullying of <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a>Q youth and <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullying</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-421">&#91;421&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears_discography" title="Britney Spears discography">Britney Spears discography</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_recorded_by_Britney_Spears" title="List of songs recorded by Britney Spears">songs</a></div>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/...Baby_One_More_Time_(album)" title="...Baby One More Time (album)">...Baby One More Time</a></i> (1999)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Oops!..._I_Did_It_Again_(album)" title="Oops!... I Did It Again (album)">Oops!... I Did It Again</a></i> (2000)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Britney_(album)" title="Britney (album)">Britney</a></i> (2001)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Zone" title="In the Zone">In the Zone</a></i> (2003)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Blackout_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Blackout (Britney Spears album)">Blackout</a></i> (2007)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Circus_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Circus (Britney Spears album)">Circus</a></i> (2008)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Femme_Fatale_(Britney_Spears_album)" title="Femme Fatale (Britney Spears album)">Femme Fatale</a></i> (2011)</li>
